PREFACE

_________

(<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1733302284111101-removebg-preview__1-removebg-preview-removebg-preview.png"/>)MONG the priceless teachings that may be foundin the great Hindu poem of the Mah√¢bh√¢rata,there is none so rare and precious as this–“The Lord’sSong.” Since it fell from the divine lips of ShriKrishna on the field of battle, and stilled the surgingemotions of his disciple and friend, how many troubledhearts has it quieted and strengthened, how manyweary souls has it led to Him! It is meant to lift theaspirant from the lower levels of renunciation, whereobjects are renounced, to the loftier heights wheredesires are dead, and where the Yogi dwells in caimand ceaseless contemplation, while his body and mindare actively employed in discharging the duties thatfall to his lot in life. That the spiritual man need notbe a recluse, that union with the divine Life may beachieved and maintained in the midst of worldlyaffairs, that the obstacles to that union lie not outsideus but within us-such is the central lesson of theBHAGAVAD-GITA.

It is a scripture of Yoga; now Yoga is literallyunion, and it means harmony with the divine Law,the becoming one with the divine Life, by the subdualof all outward-going energies, To reach this, balance

must be gained, equilibrium, so that the self, joined tothe Self, shall not be affected by pleasure or pain, desireor aversion, or any of the “pairs of opposites"between which untrained selves swing backwards andforwards. Moderation is therefore the keynote of theGita, and the harmonising of all the constituents ofman, till they vibrate in perfect attunement with theOne, the Supreme Self. This is the aim the disciple isto set before him. He must learn not to be attractedby the attractive, nor repelled by the repellent, butmust see both as manifestations of the one Lord, sothat they may be lessons for his guidance, not fettersfor his bondage. In the midst of turmoil he must restin the Lord of Peace, discharging every duty to thefullest, not because he seeks the results of his actions,but because it is his duty to perform them. His heartis an altar, love to his Lord the flame burning upon it;all his acts, physical and mental, are sacrifices offeredon the altar; and once offered, he has with them nofurther concern,

As though to make the lesson more impressive, itwas given on a field of battle. Arjuna, the warrior-prince, was to vindicate his brother’s title, to destroya usurper who was oppressing the land; it was hisduty as prince, as warrior, to fight for the deliveranceof his nation and to restore order and peace. To makethe contest more bitter, loved comrades and friendsstood on both sides, wringing his heart with personalanguish, and making a conflict of duties as well asphysical strife. Could he slay those to whom heowed love and duty, and trample on ties of kindred ?

To break family ties was a sin; to leave the people incruel bondage was a sin; where was the right way?Justice must be done, else law would be disregarded;but how slay without sin? The answer is the burdenof the book: Have no personal interest in the event;carry out the duty imposed by the position in life,realise that Ishvara, at once Lord and Law is thedoer, working out the mighty evolution that ends inbliss and peace; be identified with Him by devotion,and then perform duty as duty, fighting withoutpassion or desire, without anger or hatred; thusactivity forges no bonds, Yoga is accomplished andthe soul is free.

Such is the obvious teaching of this sacred book.But as all the acts of an Avat√¢ra are symbolical, wemay pass from the outer to the inner planes, and seein the fight of Kurukshetra the battlefield of the soul,and in the sons of Dhritar√¢shtra enemies it meets inits progress; Arjuna becomes the type of the struggling soul of the disciple, and shri Krishna is the Logosof the soul. Thus the teaching of the ancient battlefield gives guidance in all later days, and trains theaspiring soul in treading the steep and thorny paththat leads to peace. To all such souls in East andWest come these divine lessons, for the path is one,though it has many names, and all souls seek thesame goal, though they may not realise their unity.

In order to preserve the precision of the Sanskrit, afew technical terms have been given in the original infoot-notes; Manah is the mind, both in the lowermental processes in which it is swayed by the senses,

by passions and emotions, and in the higher processesof reasoning; Buddhi is the faculty above the ratiocinating mind, and is the Pure Reason, exercising thediscriminative faculty of intuition, of spiritual discernment; if these original words are not known tothe reader, the BHAGAVAD GITA loses much of itspractical value as a treatise on Yoga, and the wouldbe learner becomes confused.

The epithets applied to Shri Krishna and Arjuna‚Äì the variety of which is so characteristic of Sanskritconversation-are for the most part left untranslated,as being musical they thus add to the literary charm,whereas the genius of English is so different from thatof Sanskrit, that the many-footed epithets becomesometimes almost grotesque in translation. Namesderived from that of an ancestor, as Partha, meaningthe son of Prith√¢, Kaunteya, meaning the son ofKunt√Æ, are used in one form or the other, according tothe rhythm of the sentence. One other trifling matter,which is yet not trifling if it aids the student: whenAtm means the One Self, the SELF of all, it is printedin small capitals; where it means the lower, thepersonal self, it is printed in ordinary type; this isdone because there is sometimes a play on the word,and it is difficult for an untrained reader to follow themeaning without some such assistance. The wordBrahman, the ONE, the Supreme, is throughout translated the “ETERNAL” The word “Deva,” literally"Shining One,” is thus translated throughout. Theuse of the Western word “God” a like for “Brahman"and for the “Devas” is most misleading; the Hindu

never uses the one for the other, and never blurs theunity of the Supreme by the multiplicity of ministering Intelligences.

My wish, in adding this translation to those alreadybefore the public, was to preserve the spirit of theoriginal, especially in its deeply devotional tone, whileat the same time giving an accurate translation,reflecting the strength and the terseness of theSanskrit. In order that mistakes, due to my imperfectknowledge, might be corrected, all of this translationhas passed through the hands of one or other of thefollowing gentlemen-friends of mine at Benares ‚Äì towhom I here tender my grateful acknowledgments:B√¢bus Pramada Das Mitra, Gang√¢nath Jh√¢, K√¢liCharan Mitra, and Upendranath Basu. A few of thenotes are also due to them. In the third and fourtheditions I have also been much helped by B√¢buBhagav√¢n D√¢s, to whom I add my cordial thanks.

ANNIE BESANT.

NOTE TO THE FIRST EDITION.

____________

It has long been my ambition to place within theeasy reach of the English-reading public a cheapedition of the Bhagavad-Gita with the text inDevanagari and an English translation of the same.Mrs. Annie Besant, that warm and tried friend ofIndia whose services to our land it were vain tocount, has enabled me to realise that ambition bygenerously granting the use of her English translation. It is devoutly hoped that this great scriptureof the Hindus will find a place in thousands of homesboth in India and elsewhere.

Nov. 1907.

G. A. NATESAN

‡§∏ ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑‡•ã ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§

  1. Dharma; this is a wide word, primarily meaningthe essential nature of a thing, that which makes it tobe what it is externally: hence, the laws of its being,its duty and it includes religious rites, appropriateto those laws, customs, also righteousness.

‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡•à‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡•à‡§É‡•§

By these caste-confusing misdeeds of the slayersof the family, the everlasting caste customs*24 andfamily customs24are abolished.(43)

‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡••‡•™‡•™‡••

The abode of the men whose family customs*24are extinguished, O Jar √¢rdana, is everlastingly inhell. Thus have we heard. (44)

‡§Ö‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§¨‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ã‡§≠‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•™‡•´‡••

Alas! in committing a great sin are we engaged, we who are endeavouring to kill our kindredfrom greed of the pleasures of kingship. (45)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∞‡§£‡•á ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•¨‡••

If the sons of Dhritar√¢shtra, weapon in hand,should slay me, unresisting, unarmed, in thebattle, that would for me be the better. (46)

‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∞‡§•‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∂‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§É‡••‡•™‡•≠‡••

Sanjaya said :

Having thus spoken on the battle-field, Arjunasank down on the seat of the chariot, castingaway his bow and arrow, his mind overborne bygrief. (47)

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§

Thus in the glorious Upanishads of the BHAGAVADGITA, the science of the ETERNAL, the scripture ofYoga, the dialogue between Shri Krishna and Arjuna,the first discourse, entitled :

THE DESPONDENCY OF ARJUNA.

__________

SECOND DISCOURSE.

‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Ä‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É‡••‡•ß‡••

Sanjaya said :

To him thus with pity overcome, with smartingbrimming eyes, despondent, Madhus√ªdana spakethese words: (1)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡••‡•®‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

Whence hath this dejection befallen thee inthis perilous strait, ignoble25,heaven-closing26,infamous, O Arjuna?(2)

‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•à‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§®‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡••‡•©‡••

Yield not to impotence, O Partha ! it doth notbefit thee, Shake off this paltry faint-hearted-ness ! Stand up, Parantapa27! (3)

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§®‡•§
‡§á‡§∑‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§®‡••‡•™‡••

Arjuna said :

How, O Madhus√ªdana, shall I attack Bh√Æshmaand Drona with arrows in battle, they who areworthy of reverence, O slayer of foes ? (4)

‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§®‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§™‡•Ä‡§π ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡•§
‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡•à‡§µ
‡§≠‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•´‡••

Better in this world to eat even the beggar’scrust than to slay these most noble Gurus.Slaying these Gurus, our well-wishers,28¬πI shouldtaste of blood-besprinkled feasts.(5)

‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É
‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•á ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•¨‡••

Nor know I which for us be the better, thatwe conquer them or they conquer us-these,whom having slain we should not care to live,even these arrayed against us, the sons of Dhrita-r√¢shtra. (6)

‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡•ã‡§™‡§π‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É
‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§

1.More often translated, ‚Äúdesirous of wealth,‚Äù butthe word is used elsewhere for well-wisher, “desirousof good,” and the term is more in accordance with thetone of Arjuna’s remarks.

‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á
‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•≠‡••

My heart is weighed down with the vice offaintness; my mind is confused as to duty24.I askthee which may be the better‚Äîthat tell medecisively. I am thy disciple, suppliant to Thee ;teach me.(7)

‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§®‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç-
‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ã‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•Æ‡••

For I see not that it would drive away thisanguish that withers up my senses, if I shouldattain unrivalled monarchy on earth, or even thesovereignty of the Shining Ones.(8)

‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§°‡§æ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ ‡§π‡••‡•Ø‡••

Sanjaya said :

Gud√¢kesha, conqueror of his foes, having thusaddressed Hrish√Ækesha and said to Govinda,“I will not fight !”, became silent. (9)

‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Ä‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ö‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••

Then Hrish√ékesha, smiling, as it were, O Bh√¢rata, spake these words to him, despondent, in themidst of the two armies:(10)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§∏‡•á‡•§
‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡§ó‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

Thou grievest for those that should not be griev-

ed for, yet speakest words of wisdom29.* The wisegrieve neither for the living nor for the dead. (11)

‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••

Nor at any time verily was I not, nor thou,nor these princes of men, nor verily shall we evercease to be, hereafter, (12)

‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á ‡§ï‡•å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••

As the dweller in the body experienceth in thebody childhood, youth, old age, so passeth ho onto another body; the steadfast one grieveth notthereat.(13)

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§¶‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡••‡•ß‡•™‡••

The contacts of matter, O son of Kunt√Æ, givingcold and heat, pleasure and pain, they come andgo, impermanent; endure them bravely, OBh√¢rata.(14)

‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§® ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•´‡••

The man whom these torment not, O chief ofmen, balanced in pain and pleasure, steadfast, heis fitted for immortality.(15)

‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡••

The unreal hath no being; the real neverceaseth to be; the truth about both hath beenperceived by the seers of the essence of things30.(16)

‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•≠‡••

Know THAT to be indestructible by whom allNor can any work the destructhis is pervaded.tion of that imperishable One.(17)

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡••‡•ß‡•Æ‡••

These bodies of the embodied One, who iseternal, indestructible and immeasurable, areknown as finite. Therefore fight, O Bh√¢rata. (18)

‡§Ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§≠‡•å ‡§§‡•å ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•Ø‡••

He who regardeth this31as a slayer, and hewho thinketh he is slain, both of them are ignorant. He slayeth not, nor is he slain.(19)

‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø-
‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã
‡§® ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡••‡•®‡•¶‡••

He is not born, nor doth he die; nor havingbeen, ceaseth he any more to be; unborn, perpetual, eternal and ancient, he is not slain when thebody is slaughtered.(20)

‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ò‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡••

Who knoweth him indestructible, perpetual,unborn, undiminishing, how can that man slay,O P√¢rtha, or cause to be slain? (21)

‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø
‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ -
‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•Ä‡••‡•®‡•®‡••

As a man, casting off worn-out garments, takethnew ones, so the dweller in the body, casting offworn-out bodies, entereth into others that arenew.(22)

‡§®‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§π‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ã ‡§® ‡§∂‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡••‡•®‡•©‡••

Weapons cleave him not, nor fire burneth him,nor waters wet him, nor winddrieth him away. (23)

‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§£‡•Å‡§∞‡§ö‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§É‡••‡•®‡•™‡••

Uncleavable he, incombustible he, and indeedneither to be wetted nor dried away; perpetual,all-pervasive, stable, immovable, ancient.(24)

‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•´‡••

Unmanifest, unthinkable, immutable, he iscalled; therefore knowing him as such, thoushouldst not grieve.(25)

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•¨‡••

Or if thou thinkest of him as being constantly

born and constantly dying, even then, O mightyarmed, thou shouldst not grieve.(26)

‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•≠‡••

For certain is death for the born, and certainis birth for the dead; therefore over the inevitable thou shouldst not grieve. (27)

‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡••‡•®‡•Æ‡••

Beings are unmanifest in their origin, manifestin their midmost state, O Bh√¢rata, unmanifestlikewise are they in dissolution. What roomthen for lamentation?(28)

‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§®-
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡§ø
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•Ø‡••

As marvellous one regardeth him; as marvellous another speaketh thereof; asmarvellousanother heareth thereof; yet having heard noneindeed understandeth.(29)

‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•Ä ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•¶‡••

This dweller in the body of everyone is everinvulnerable, O Bh√¢rata; therefore thou shouldstnot grieve for any creature.(30)

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•©‡•ß‡••

Further, looking to thine own duty24thoushouldst not tremble; for there is nothing morewelcome to a Kshattriya32than righteous war.(31)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§≤‡§≠‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡•®‡••

Happy the Kshattriyas, O P√¢rtha, who obtainsuch a fight, offered unsought as an open door toheaven,(32)

‡§Ö‡§•‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•©‡••

But if thou wilt not carry on this righteouswarfare, then casting away thine own duty24andthino honour, thou wilt incur cin.(33)

‡§Ö‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•©‡•™‡••

Mon will recount thy perpetual dishonour,and, to one highly esteemed, dishonour exceedethdeath.(34)

‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§•‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§≤‡§æ‡§ò‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡•´‡••

The great car-warriors33will think thee fled from

the battle from fear, and thou, that wast highlythought of by them, wilt be lightly held.(35)

‡§Ö‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¨‡§π‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡•¨‡••

Many unseemly words will be spoken by thineenemies, slandering thy strength; what morepainful than that?(36)

‡§π‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§É‡••‡•©‡•≠‡••

Slain, thou wilt obtain heaven ; victorious,thou wilt enjoy the earth; therefore stand up, Oson of Kunt√Æ, resolute to fight.(37)

‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡•å ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•å‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•Æ‡••

Taking as equal pleasure and pain, gain andloss, victory and defeat, gird thee for the battle;thus thou shalt not incur sin.(38)

‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡•§
‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•Ø‡••

This teaching set forth to thee is in accordancewith the S√¢√±khya34; hear it now according to theYoga35, imbued with which teaching, O P√¢rtha,thou shalt cast away the bonds of action.(39)

‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•¶‡••

In this there is no loss of effort, nor is theretransgression. Even a little of this knowledge24protects from great fear. (40)

‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡•á‡§π ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•§
‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•ß‡••

The determinate Reason36is but one-pointed,

O joy of the Kurus; many-branched and endlessare the thoughts of the irresolute.(41)

‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••‡•™‡•®‡••

Flowery speech is uttered by the foolish, rejoicing in the letter of the Vedas37,O P√¢rtha,saying : ‚Äú There is naught but this‚Äù; (42)

‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§™‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡•©‡••

With desire for self38, with heaven for goal,they offer birth as the fruit of action, and prescribe many and various ceremonies for the attainment of pleasure and lordship.(43)

‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•å ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•™‡•™‡••

For them who cling to pleasure and lordship,whose minds are captivated by such teaching, isnot designed this determinate Reason39,on contemplation40steadily bent.¬π41 (44)

‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•´‡••

The Vedas deal with the three attributes42; be

1.The following alternative translation of Slokas 42,43, and 44 is offered: “The flowery speech that theunwise utter, O P√¢rtha, clinging to the word of theVeda, saying there is nothing else, ensouled by desireand longing after heaven, (the speech) that offerethonly rebirth as the (ultimate) fruit of action, that isfull of (recommendations to) various rites for thesake of (gaining) enjoyments and sovereignty-thethought of those misled by that (speech), cleaving topleasures and lordship, not being inspired with resolution, is not engaged in contemplation.” This is closerto the original, which is all in one sentence.

thou above these three attributes, O Arjuna ; beyond the pairs of opposites, ever steadfast in purity43,careless of possessions, full of the SELF, (45)

‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§â‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡§ï‡•á‡•§

Thy business is with the action only, neverwith its fruits; so let not the fruit of actionbe thy motive, nor be thou to inaction attached.(47)

Perform action, O Dhananjaya, dwelling inunion with the divine45,renouncing attachmentsand balanced evenly in success and failure: equilibrium is called yoga.(48)

Far lower than the Yoga of Discrimination46 of Atma”)is action, O Dhananjaya. Take thou refuge inthe Pure Reason39; pitiable are they who workfor fruit. (49)

United to the Pure Reason39one abandonethhere both good and evil deeds; therefore cleavethou to yoga ; yoga is skill in action.(50)

The Sages, united to the Pure Reason39,

renounce the fruit which action yieldeth, and,liberated from the bonds of birth, they go tothe blissful seat.(51)

When thy mind39shall escape from this tangleof delusion, then thou shalt rise to indifference asto what has been heard and shall be heard.(52)

passion, fear and anger, is called a sage53of stablemind50.(56)

He who on every side is without attachments,whatever hap of fair and foul, who neither likesnor dislikes, of such a one the understanding54iswell poised.(57)

When, again, as a tortoise draws in on all sidesits limbs, he withdraws his senses from the objects of sense, then is his understanding49wellpoised.(58)

The objects of sense, but not the relish forthem55, turn away from an abstemious dweller inthe body; and even relish tu neth away from himafter the Supreme is seen.(59)

O son of Kunt√Æ, the excited senses of even awise man, though he be striving, impetuouslycarry away his mind51.(60)

‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§É‡•§

Having restrained them all, he should sit harmonised, I his supreme goal; for, whose sensesare mastered, of him the understanding49is wellpoised.(61)

‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Ç‡§™‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•¨‡•®‡••

Man, musing on the objects of sense, conceiveth an attachment to these; from attachment ariseth desire ; from desire anger56cometh forth ; (62)

‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡•©‡••

From anger proceedeth delusion; from delusion confused memory; from confused memory the destruction of Reason57from_destruction of Reason he perishes.(63)

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø ‡••‡•¨‡•™‡••

But the disciplined self, moving among sense objects with senses free from attraction and re-pulsion, mastered by the Self, goeth to peace. ( 64 )

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§

In that Peace the extinction of all pains ariseth for him, for of him whose heart58is peace-ful the Reason59soon attaineth equilibrium. (65)

‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡•§

There is no Pure Reason for the non-harmo-nised, nor for the non-harmonised is there concentration60 for him without concentration there is no peace, and for the unpeaceful how can there be happiness? (66)

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡•≠‡••

Such of the roving senses as the mind61yieldeth to, that hurries away the understanding62just

as the gale hurries away a ship upon the waters. (67)

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡••‡•¨‡•Æ‡••

Therefore, O mighty-armed, whose senses are all completely restrained from the objects of sense, of him the understanding is well poised.(68)

‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Ä‡•§

That which is the night of all beings, for the disciplined man is the time of waking; when other beings are waking, then is it night for the sage who seeth63*(69)

‡§Ü‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§ö‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

___________________________________________

* sage is awake to things over which the ordi-nary man sleeps and the eyes of the sage are open to truths shut out from the common vision, while vice versa that which is real for the masses is illusion for the sage.

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á
‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡••‡•≠‡•¶‡••

He attaineth Peace, into whom all desires flow as rivers flow into the ocean, which is filled with water, but remaineth unmoved‚Äînot he who desireth desires.(70)

‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•≠‡•ß‡••

Whoso forsaketh all desires and goeth onwards free from yearnings, selfless and without egoism‚Äî he goeth to Peace.(71)

‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§®‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•≠‡•®‡••

This is the ETERNAL state, O son of Prith√¢. Having attained thereto, none is bewildered. Who, even at the death-hour, is established theren,he goeth to the Nirv√¢na of the ETERNAL (72)

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡•¶ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É‡••

Thus in the glorious Upanishads of the BHAGAVAD GITA, the science of the ETERNAL, the scripture of Yoga, the dialogue between Sri Krishna and Arjuna, the second discourse, entitled:

YOGA BY THE SANKHYA.

____________

THIRD DISCOURSE

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡••‡•ß‡••

Arjuna said :

If it be thought by Thee that knowledge is superior to action, O Jan√¢rdana, why dost Thou, O Keshava, enjoin on me this terrible action ? (1)

‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§¶ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•®‡••

With these perplexing words Thou only confusest my understanding64therefore tell me with certainty the one way by which I may reach bliss.(2)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡§ò‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

In this world there is a twofold path, as I before said, O sinless one that of yoga by know- ledge, of the S√¢√±khyas ; and that of yoga by action, of the Yogis.(3)

‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡••

Man winneth not freedom from action by abstaining from activity, nor by mere renunciation doth he rise to perfection.(4)

‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∂‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§É‡••‡•´‡••

Nor can anyone, even for an instant, remain really actionless; for helplessly is everyone driven to action by the qualities65born of nature66. (5)

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•¨‡••

Who sitteth, controlling the organs of action, but dwelling in his mind* on the objects of the senses, that bewildered man is called a hypocrite. (6)

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§≠‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•§
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•≠‡••

But who, controlling the senses by the mind67O Arjuna, with the organs of action without attachment, performeth yoga by action68, he is worthy,(7)

‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É‡••‡•Æ‡••

Perform thou right69 action, for, action is rior to inaction, and, inactive, even the maintenance of thy body would not be possible.(8)

‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡••‡•Ø‡••

The world is bound by action, unless performed for the sake of sacrifice; for that sake, free from attachment, O son of Kunt√Æ, perform thou action.(9)

‡§∏‡§π‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••

Having in ancient times emanated mankind together with sacrifice, the Lord of emanation70said: " By this shall ye propagate; be this to you the giver of desire71 (10)

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

“With this nourish ye the Shining Ones, and

may the Shining Ones nourish you; thus nourishing one another ye shall reap the supremest good. (11)

‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••

‚ÄúFor, nourished by sacrifice, the Shining Ones shall bestow on you the enjoyments you desire.” A thief verily is he who enjoyeth what is given by Them without returning Them aught.(12)

‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§∑‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••

The righteous, who eat the remains of the sacrifice, are freed from all sins; but the impious, who dress food for their own sakes, they verily eat sin.(13)

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•™‡••

From food creatures become; from rain is the

production of food; rain proceedeth from sacrifice; sacrifice ariseth out of action.(14)

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•´‡••

Know thou that from Brahma72action groweth, and Brahma from the Imperishable cometh. Therefore the ETERNAL, the all-permeating, is ever present in sacrifice.(15)

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§π ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ò‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡••

He who on earth doth not follow the wheel thus revolving, sinful of life and rejoicing in the senses, he, O son of Pritha, liveth in vain.(16)

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•É‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•≠‡••

But the man who rejoiceth in the SELF, with

the SELF is satisfied, and is content in the SELF, for him verily there is nothing to do ;(17)

‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§π ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•Æ‡••

For him there is no interest in things done, in this world, nor any in things not done, nor doth any object of his depend on any being.(18)

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•Ø‡••

Therefore, without attachment, constantly perform action which is duty, for, by performing action without attachment, man verily reacheth the Supreme.(19)

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•à‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§ú‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•¶‡••

Janaka and others indeed attained to perfection by action then having an eye to the welfare of he world also, thou shouldst perform action. (20)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•ß‡••

Whatsoever a great man doeth, that other men also do; the standard he setteth up, by that the people go.(21)

‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•®‡••

There is nothing in the three worlds, O P√¢rtha, that should be done by Me, nor anything un- attained that might be attained; yet I mingle in action.(22)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡••‡•®‡•©‡••

For if I mingled not ever in action unwearied, men all around would follow My path, O son of Prith√¢.(23)

‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•®‡•™‡••

These worlds would fall into ruin, if I did not perform action; I should be the author of confusion of castes, and should destroy these creatures,(24)

‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•´‡••

As the ignorant act from attachment to action, O Bh√¢rata, so should the wise act without attachment, desiring the welfare of the world.(25)

‡§® ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ú‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•¨‡••

Let no wise man unsettle the mind of ignorant people attached to action; but acting in harmony with Mo let him render all action attractive. (26)

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•≠‡••

All actions are wrought by the quali-

ties65 of nature only. The self, deluded by egoism73thinketh: “I am the doer."(27)

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡••‡•®‡•Æ‡••

But he, O mighty-armed, who knoweth the essence of the divisions of the qualities and functions, holding that “the qualities move amid the qualities74is not attached.(28)

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡••‡•®‡•Ø‡••

Those deluded by the qualities of nature are attached to the functions of the qualities. The man of perfect knowledge should not unsettle the foolish whose knowledge is imperfect.(29)
______________________________________________

+qualities, as sense-organs move amid the Gunas, qualities, as sense-objects. A suggested reading is “The functions dwell in the propensities.” Sankar√¢ch√¢rya says, “of the class of qualities and the class of actions;” or the arrangement, or relations of qualities and actions.

‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡••‡•©‡•¶‡••

Surrendering all actions to Me, with thy thoughts resting on the supreme SELF, from hope and egoism freed, and of mental fever cured, engage in battle.(30)

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••‡•©‡•ß‡••

Who abide ever in this teaching of Mine full of faith and free from caviling, they too are released from actions.(31)

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§É‡••‡•©‡•®‡••

Who carp at My teaching and act not thereon, senseless, deluded in all knowledge, know thou these mindlees ones as fated to be destroyed. (32)

‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•©‡••

Even the man of knowledge behaves in confor mity with his own nature; beings follow nature’; what shall restraint avail ?(33)

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•å ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§µ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§®‡•å‡••‡•©‡•™‡••

Affection and aversion for the objects of sense abide in the senses; let none come under the dominion of these two they are obstructors of the path.(34)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§É‡••‡•©‡•´‡••

Better one’s own duty75though destitute of merit, than the duty75 of another, well discharged. Better death in the discharge of one’s own duty ;* the duty* of another is full of danger.(35)

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••‡•©‡•¨‡••

Arjuna said :

But dragged on by what does a man commit

sin, reluctantly indeed, O Varshneya, as it were by force constrained?(36)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§∞‡§ú‡•ã‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡•≠‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

It is desire, it is wrath, begotten by the quality of motion76all-consuming, all-polluting, know thou this as our foe here on earth.(37)

‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§≤‡•ç‡§¨‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡•Æ‡••

As a flame is enveloped by smoke, as a mirror by dust, as an embryo is wrapped by the amnion, so This77 is enveloped by it.(38)

‡§Ü‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡••‡•©‡•Ø‡••

______________________________________________

“THIS” as opposed to “THAT " theETERNAL. Some say “THIS” stands for knowledge.

Enveloped is wisdom by this constant enemy of the wise in the form of desire, which is insatiable as a flame,(39)

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§è‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•¶‡••

The senses, the mind* and the Reasonare said to be its seat; by these enveloping wisdom, it bewilders the dweller in the body.(40)

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•§
‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•ß‡••

Therefore, O best of the Bh√¢ratas, mastering first the senses, do thou slay this thing of sin, destructive of wisdom and knowledge.(41)

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§É‡••‡•™‡•®‡••

It is said that the senses are great; greater than the senses is the mind78greater than the mind is the Reason59but what is greater than the Reason59is He79 (42

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•™‡•©‡••

Thus understanding Him as greater than the Reason80restraining the self by the SELF, slay thou, O mighty-armed, “the enemy in the form of desire, difficult to overcome.(43)

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§™‡•¶ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§

Thus in the glorious Upanishads of the BHAGAVAD GITA, the science of the ETERNAL, the scripture of Yoga, the dialogue between Sri Krishna and Arjuna, the third discourse, entitled:

THE YOGA OF ACTION.

_______________

FOURTH DICOURSE

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§á‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§π‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡§µ‡•á‡§Ω‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

This imperishable yoga I declared to Vivasv√¢n; Vivasv√¢n taught it to Manu; Manu to Ikshv√¢ku told it.(1)

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§π ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡••‡•®‡••

This, handed on down the line, the King-Sages knew. This yoga by great efflux of time decayed in the world, O Parantapa.(2)

‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•©‡••

This same ancient yoga hath been to-day declared to thee by Me, for thou art My devotee and My friend; it is the supreme Secret. (3)

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡••

Arjuna said :

Later was Thy birth, earlier the birth of Vivasv√¢n; how then am I to understand that Thou declaredst it in the beginning?(4)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§¨‡§π‡•Ç‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§• ‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡••‡•´‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

Many births have been left behind by Me and by thee, O Arjuna. I know them all, but thou knowest not thine, O Parantapa.(5)

‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡••‡•¨‡••

Though unborn, the imperishable SELF, and also the Lord of all beings, brooding over nature

which is Mine own, yet I am born through My own_Power81 (6)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•≠‡••

Whenever there is decay of righteousness82O Bh√¢rata, and there is exaltation of unrighteousness83then I Myself come forth ;(7)

‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡•á ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡•á‡••‡•Æ‡••

For the protection of the good, for the destrution of evil-doers, for the sake of firmly establishing righteousness82I am born from age to age. (8)

‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡•§

____________________________________________

the power of thought that produces form, which is transient and therefore unreal compared with the eternal Reality; hence M√¢y√¢ comes to be taken as the power of producing illusion.

the opposite of dharma, all that is dis-orderly, against the nature of things.

‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡•à‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡••‡•Ø‡••

He who thus knoweth My divine birth and action, in its essence, having abandoned the body, cometh not to birth again, but cometh unto Me, O Arjuna. (9)

‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§≠‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡§π‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••

Freed from passion, fear and anger, filled with Me, taking refuge in Me, purified in the fire84 of wisdom, many have entered into My Being.(10)

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

However men approach Me, even so do I wel-come them, for the path men take from every side is Mine, O P√¢rtha. (11)

‡§ï‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§π ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••

They who long after success in action on earth worship the Shining Ones ; for in brief space verily, in this world of men, success is born of action. (12)

‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••

The four castes were emanated by Me, by the different distribution of qualities65 and actions ; know Me to be the author of them, though the actionless and inexhaustible. (13)

‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡••‡•ß‡•™‡••

Nor do actions affect Me, nor is the fruit of action desired by Me. He who thus knoweth Me is not bound by actions. (14)

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•´‡••

Having thus known, our forefathers, ever seek-ing liberation, performed action; therefore do thou also perform action, as did our forefathers in the olden time. (15)

‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á‡§Ω‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡••

‚Äú What is action, what inaction “? Even the wise are herein perplexed. Therefore I will declare to thee the action by knowing which thou shalt be loosed from evil. (16)

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§π‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•≠‡••

It is needful to discriminate action, to dis-criminate unlawful action, and to discriminate inaction ; mysterious is the path of action. (17)

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•Æ‡••

He who seeth inaction in action, and action in inaction, he is wise among men, he is har-monious, even while performing all action.(18)

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•Ø‡••

Whose works are all free from the moulding of desire, whose actions are burned up by the fire of wisdom, him the wise have called a Sage.( 19 )

‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•É‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§É‡••‡•®‡•¶‡••

Having abandoned attachment to the fruit of action, always content, nowhere seeking refuge, he is not doing anything, although doing actions.(20)

‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡••

Hoping for naught, his mind and self control-led, having abandoned all greed, performing action by the body alone, he doth not commit sin. (21)

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•å ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•®‡••

Content with whatsoever he obtaineth without effort, free from the pairs of opposites, without envy, balanced in success and failure, though acting.he is not bound.(22)

‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•©‡••

Of one with attachment dead, harmonious, with his thoughts established in wisdom, his works sacrifices, all action melts away.(23)

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•å ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡••‡•®‡•™‡••

The ETERNAL the oblation, the ETERNAL the clarified butter, are offered in the ETERNAL the

fire by the ETERNAL; unto the ETERNAL verily shall he go who in his action meditateth wholly upon the ETERNAL85 (24)

‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•´‡••

Some Yogis offer up sacrifice to the Shining Ones86others sacrifice only by pouring sacrifice into the fire of the ETERNAL ;(25)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•®‡•¨‡••

Some pour as sacrifice hearing and the other senses into the fires of restraint; some pour sound and the other objects of sense into the fires of the senses as sacrifice; (26)

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•å ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•≠‡••

Others again into the wisdom-kindled fire of union attained by self-control, pour as sacrifice all the functions of the senses and the functions oflife ;(27)

‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•®‡•Æ‡••

Yet others the sacrifice of wealth, the sacrifice of austerity, the sacrifice of yoga, the sacrifice of silent reading and wisdom, men concentrated and of effectual vows;(28)

‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§ó‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•®‡•Ø‡••

Yet others pour as sacrifice the outgoing breath in the incoming, and the incoming in the out- going, restraining the flow of the outgoing and

incoming breaths, solely absorbed in the control of breathing87 (29)

‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•©‡•¶‡••

Others regular in food, pour as sacrifice their life-breaths in life-breaths. All these are know-ers of sacrifice, and by sacrifice have destroyed their sins.(30)

‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡••‡•©‡•ß‡••

The eaters of the life-giving88 remains of sacrifice go to the changeless ETERNAL. This world is not for the non-sacrificer, much less the other, O best of the Kurus. (31)

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•á‡•§
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á‡••‡•©‡•®‡••

Many and various sacrifices are thus spread out before the ETERNAL89Know thou that all these are born of action, and thus knowing thou shalt be free. (32)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•©‡•©‡••

Better than the sacrifice of any objects is the sacrifice of wisdom, O Parantapa. All actions in their entirety, O P√¢rtha, culminate in wisdom.(33)

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••‡•©‡•™‡••

Learn thou this by discipleship90by investiga-

tion, and by service. The wise, the seers of the essence of things, will instruct thee in wisdom. (34)

‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•á‡§£ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•´‡••

And having known this, thou shalt not again fall into this confusion, O P√¢ndava; for by this thou wilt see all beings without exception in the SELF, and thus in Me.(35)

‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡•É‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•¨‡••

Even if thou art the most sinful of all sinners, yet shalt thou cross over all sin by the raft of wisdom.(36)

‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡••‡•©‡•≠‡••

As the burning fire reduces fuel to ashes, O Arjuna, so doth the fire of wisdom reduce all actions to ashes.(37)

‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•Æ‡••

Verily there is no purifier in this world like wisdom; he that is perfected in yoga finds it in the SELF in due season.(38)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§Å‡§≤‡§≠‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡•Ø‡••

The man who is full of faith91obtaineth wisdom, and he also who hath mastery over his senses; and, having obtained wisdom, he goeth swiftly to the supreme Peace.(39)

‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡•ã ‡§® ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••‡•™‡•¶‡••

But the ignorant, faithless, doubting self goeth to destruction ; nor this world, nor that beyond,nor happiness, is there for the doubting self. (40)

‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡••‡•™‡•ß‡••

He who hath renounced actions by yoga, who hath cloven asunder doubt by wisdom, who is ruled by the SELF92actions do not bind him, O Dhananjaya. (41)

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§õ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡••‡•™‡•®‡••

Therefore, with the sword of the wisdom of the SELF cleaving asunder this ignorance-born doubt dwelling in thy heart, be established in yoga, Stand up, O. Bharata. (42)

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§™‡•¶ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä-
‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§

Thus in the glorious Upanishads of the BHAGAVAD-GITA, the science of the ETERNAL, the scripture of Yoga the dialogue between Shri Krishna and Arjuna, the fourth discourse, entitled :

THE YOGA OF WISDOM.

_______

FIFTH DISCOURSE

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø ‡§è‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡••

Arjuna said :

Renunciation of actions Thou praisest, O Krishna, and then also yoga. Of the two which one is the better? That tell me conclusively. (1)

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡•Å‡§≠‡•å‡•§
‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡••

The Blessed Lord said:

Renunciation and yoga by action both lead to the highest bliss; of the two, yoga by action is verily better than renunciation of action.(2)

‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•©‡••

He should be known as a perpetual ascetic93who neither hateth nor desireth; free from the pairs of opposites, O mighty-armed, he is easily set free from bondage.(3)

‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•å ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡•á ‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•™‡••

Children, not sages, speak of the S√¢ukhya94 and the Yoga95 as different; he who is duly esta-blished in one obtaineth the fruits of both.(4)

‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•´‡••

That place which is gained by the S√¢nkhyas is reached by the Yog√Æs also. He seeth, who seeth that the S√¢nkhya and the Yoga are one.(5)

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§® ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡••

But without yoga, O mighty-armed, renun-ciation is hard to attain to; the yoga-harmonised Muni swiftly goeth to the ETERNAL.(6)

‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•≠‡••

He who is harmonised by yoga, the self puri-fied, SELF-ruled, the senses subdued, whose SELF is the SELF of all beings, although acting he is not affected.(7)

‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•Æ‡••

“I do not anything,” should think the harmo.. nised one, who knoweth the essence of things; seeing, hearing, touching, smelling, eating, moving, sleeping, breathing.(8)

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•Ø‡••

Speaking, giving, grasping, opening and closing

the eyes, he holdeth: “The senses move among the objects of the senses."(9)

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡§æ‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••

He who acteth, placing all actions in the E:ERNAL, abandoning attachment, is unaffected by sin as a lotus leaf by the waters.(10)

‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

Yogis, having abandoned attachment, perform action only by the body, by the mind51by theReason59 ‚Ä†, and even by the senses, for the purifi cation of the self. (11)

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§´‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••

The harmonised man, having abandoned the fruit of action, attaineth to the eternal Peace;

the non-harmonised, impelled by desire, atticbed to fruit, are bound.(12)

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∂‡•Ä‡•§
‡§®‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•Ä ‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••

Mentally renouncing all actions, the sovereign dweller in the body resteth serenely in the nine gated city96neither acting nor causing to act. (13)

‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•™‡••

The Lord of the world produceth not the idea of agency, nor actions, nor the union together of action and its fruit; nature, however, mani-festeth.(14)

‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•´‡••

The Lord accepteth neither the evil-doing nor

yet the well-doing of any. Wisdom is enveloped by unwisdom ; therewith mortals are deluded.(15)

‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡§¶‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡••

Verily, in whom unwisdom is destroyed by the wisdom of the SELF, in them wisdom, shining as the sun, reveals the Supreme.(16)

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ç‡§§‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•≠‡••

Thinking on THAT, merged in THAT, established in THAT, solely devoted to THAT, they go whence there is no return, their sins dispelled by wisdom.(17)

‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•á ‡§ó‡§µ‡§ø ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡•§
‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•Æ‡••

Sages look equally on a Br√¢hmana adorned

with learning and humility, a cow, an elephant, and even a dog and an outcaste97 (18)

‡§á‡§π‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•Ø‡••

Even here on earth everything is overcome by those whose mind98remains balanced; the ETER-NAL is incorruptible and balanced; therefore they are established in the ETERNAL.(19)

‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••‡•®‡•¶‡••

With Reason59 firm, unperplexed, the knower of the ETERNAL established in the ETERNAL, neither rejoiceth on obtaining what is pleasant, nor sorroweth on obtaining what is unpleasant. (20)

‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡•ß‡••

He, whose self is unattached to external con-tacts and findeth joy in the SELF, having the self harmonisel with the ETERNAL by yoga, enjoys imperishable bliss.(21)

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ú‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§Ü‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§É‡••‡•®‡•®‡••
